## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology
**Analysis**: This task models population growth rate dP_dt as a function of current population P and time t, which is a classic problem in population dynamics governed by ordinary differential equations. The relationships typically capture density-dependent regulation, environmental forcing, or intrinsic growth limitations.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (Malthusian, unlimited resources)
- Logistic growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent regulation towards carrying capacity)
- Generalized logistic (Richards): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (asymmetric sigmoid growth)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (skewed S-shaped growth, often for tumors or aging populations)
- Allee effect (cubic): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (c2 - P) (positive density dependence at low population, e.g., mate finding)
- Harvesting with logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (proportional harvesting or fishing mortality)
- Constant harvest: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (fixed quota removal)
- Time-varying carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / (c1 + c2 * t)) (environmental trend)
- Seasonally forced growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * P (periodic environmental fluctuation)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (allometric scaling of population growth)
- Exponential growth with time-decaying rate: dP_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * P (improving or deteriorating environment)
- Saturating growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P / (c1 + P) (Michaelis-Menten-like, e.g., resource limited)
- Ricker-like continuous model: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(-c1 * P) (overcompensatory density dependence)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear term in P alone indicates density-independent growth (exponential model).
- Presence of -c*P**2 or higher powers of P signals density-dependent regulation (intraspecific competition).
- Cubic function of P, especially with a small-population zero crossing, hints at an Allee effect (threshold for growth).
- Additive constant term (not multiplied by P) suggests constant harvesting or fixed immigration/mortality.
- Subtractive term proportional to P without density regulation represents proportional harvesting or natural mortality.
- Periodic functions of t (sin, cos) imply seasonal or cyclic environmental forcing on growth rate.
- Rational forms like P/(c+P) imply saturation of growth rate due to resource limitation or handling time.
- log(K/P) form indicates Gompertz-type mortality acceleration near carrying capacity, typical in tumor growth or aging cohorts.
- Exponential decay factor multiplying P suggests time-dependent deterioration of habitat or declining reproductive rate.
- Terms like (1 - (P/K)**n) generalize asymmetric growth curves where inflection point can shift.
